<div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/5759f22a-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/5759f22a-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">DISCOVERY OF FOUR DOUBLY IMAGED QUASAR LENSES FROM THE SLOAN DIGITAL SKY SURVEY</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Naohisa Inada</span><sup>1</sup></span>, <span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Masamune Oguri</span><sup>2,3</sup></span>, <span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Cristian E. class=\"overflow-y\" data-toolbar-container=\"references\"></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"nav-item wd-in-pg-toolbar-artdata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"\" class=\"nav-top-link-drop-down article-toolbar-dropdown\" data-toolbar-action=\"artdata\" data-nav-trigger=\"artdata\">Article data<span class=\"icon-arrow-down\"></span></a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D1538-3881%2F147%2F6%2F153\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">1538-3881/147/6/153</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n                      <P>We report the discovery of four doubly imaged quasar lenses. All the four systems are selected as lensed quasar candidates from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey data. We confirm their lensing hypothesis with additional imaging and spectroscopic follow-up observations. The discovered lenses are SDSS J0743+2457 with the source redshift <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 2.165, the lens redshift <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> = 0.381, and the image separation \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />034, SDSS J1128+2402 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 1.608 and \u03b8 = 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />844, SDSS J1405+0959 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 1.810, <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> \u2248 0.66, and \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />978, and SDSS J1515+1511 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 2.054, <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> = 0.742, and \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />989. It is difficult to estimate the lens redshift of SDSS J1128+2402 from the current data. Two of the four systems (SDSS J1405+0959 and SDSS J1515+1511) are included in our final statistical lens sample to derive constraints on dark energy and the evolution of massive galaxies.</P>       </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=1538-3881/147/6/153&doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014AJ....147..153I\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2014AJ....147..153I&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2014AJ....147..153I\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/1538-3881/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s1\" name=\"aj494663s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Gravitationally lensed quasars have proven to be a useful tool for a variety of astrophysical and cosmological studies, as described e.g., in Kochanek (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r28\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r28\">2006</a>). Applications of quasar lenses include constraints on cosmological parameters and measurements of mass distributions for galaxy- and cluster-scale halos, interstellar medium associated with lensing or intervening galaxies, and the structure of quasar accretion disk and outflow (e.g., Fukugita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r15\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r15\">1990</a>; Kochanek <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r27\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r27\">1991</a>; Oguri et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r36\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r36\">2013</a>; Curran et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r11\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r11\">2007</a>; Poindexter et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r40\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r40\">2008</a>; Misawa et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r30\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r30\">2013</a>). The use of these quasar lenses can be enhanced by constructing a homogeneous lens sample with a well-characterized selection function. For instance, the Cosmic Lens All Sky Survey (Myers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r32\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r32\">2003</a>; Browne et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r9\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r9\">2003</a>) has provided a complete sample of 22 strong lenses selected among ~16,000 radio sources, which has been used for a number of cosmological and astrophysical studies (e.g., Chae et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r10\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r10\">2006</a>). Currently, we have completed the SDSS Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; Oguri et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r34\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r34\">2006</a>), which is the current largest lensed quasar survey using optical data of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS; York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r49\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r49\">2000</a>). The total number of lensed quasars identified in the SDSS data is 62<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#aj494663fn1\">9</a></sup> (Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r22\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r22\">2012</a>). The statistical analysis for SQLS lenses to constrain both cosmological parameters and the evolution of massive galaxies has been reported in Oguri et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r35\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r35\">2012</a>).</p><p>In this paper, we report the discovery of four lensed quasars from the SQLS. Since the description of the four lensed quasars in Inada et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r22\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r22\">2012</a>) is so brief, we show the detailed properties of the four systems here. We briefly describe the SDSS data and our algorithm to locate lensed quasar candidates in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s2\">2</a>. We then present follow-up observations to confirm their lensing hypotheses in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s3\">3</a>. We carry out mass modeling in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s4\">4</a>. Our result is summarized in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s5\">5</a>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s2\" name=\"aj494663s2\">2.\u00a0CANDIDATE SELECTION FROM THE SLOAN DIGITAL SKY SURVEY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The SQLS identifies lensed quasars among ~100, 000 quasars (Schneider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r44\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r44\">2010</a>) from the SDSS Data Release 7 (DR7). The SDSS is a survey using a dedicated wide-field 2.5\u00a0m telescope (Gunn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r19\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r19\">2006</a>) at the Apache Point Observatory (New Mexico, USA) to conduct imaging and spectroscopic surveys for a quarter of the sky. The imaging data were obtained through five broad-band filters (<em>ugriz</em>; Fukugita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r16\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r16\">1996</a>; Gunn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r18\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r18\">1998</a>; Doi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r12\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r12\">2010</a>) with astrometric accuracy better than ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 (Pier et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r39\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r39\">2003</a>) and with photometric zeropoint accuracy better than ~0.01\u00a0mag (Hogg et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r20\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r20\">2001</a>; Smith et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r45\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r45\">2002</a>; Ivezi\u0107 et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r23\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r23\">2004</a>; Tucker et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r48\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r48\">2006</a>; Padmanabhan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r37\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r37\">2008</a>). Quasar and galaxy candidates were selected by the SDSS spectroscopic pipeline based on the imaging data (Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r13\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r13\">2001</a>; Richards et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r41\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r41\">2002</a>; Strauss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r47\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r47\">2002</a>). The candidates were tiled in each plate according to the algorithm of Blanton et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r8\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r8\">2003</a>), and were observed with multi-object fiber spectrographs (<em>R</em> ~ 1800) covering 3800\u20139200\u00a0\u00c5 (Blanton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r8\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r8\">2003</a>). The SDSS DR7 data have already been made public (Stoughton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r46\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r46\">2002</a>; Abazajian et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r1\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r1\">2003</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r2\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r2\">2004</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r3\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r3\">2005</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r4\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r4\">2009</a>; Adelman-McCarthy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r5\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r5\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r6\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r6\">2007</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r7\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r7\">2008</a>).</p><p>The procedure to identify lensed quasar candidates from the spectroscopic SDSS quasars has been described in the series of SQLS papers (e.g., Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r21\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r21\">2008</a>), which we outline here. We use two selection methods. One is to find quasars with nearby objects whose colors are similar to the quasars. This method is tagged as the \"color selection.\" The color selection does not always work well for the SDSS data because of the relatively poor spatial resolution of SDSS imaging data, whose seeing sizes are comparable to typical image separations of quasar lenses. Therefore, in order to find lenses which are not deblended into multiple components in the SDSS data, we also exploit the so-called morphological selection, in which we select spectroscopic quasars with extended morphologies as lensed quasar candidates. SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1128+2402 are selected by the morphological selection, whereas SDSS J1405+0959 and SDSS J1515+1511 are selected by both the color selection and the morphological selection. The SDSS properties of these four candidates are summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t1\">1</a>. We also show the SDSS <em>i</em>-band images of the four objects in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f1\">1</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Finding charts (SDSS <em>i</em>-band images) of the four lens systems. as quasar lenses ULAS 074352.6+245743 and ULAS 140515.4+095931, respectively, by the Major UKIDSS-SDSS Cosmic Lens Survey (MUSCLES) survey (Jackson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r24\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r24\">2012</a>). In the MUSCLES survey lens candidates are selected by cross-matching SDSS quasars with UKIDSS near-infrared images which typically have much better spatial resolution. Our identification of SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1405+0959 as lens candidates is independent of the MUSCLES survey result.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s3\" name=\"aj494663s3\">3.\u00a0FOLLOW-UP IMAGING AND SPECTROSCOPY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"aj494663s3-1\" name=\"aj494663s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Follow-up Data</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We carried out follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations using the University of Hawaii 2.2\u00a0m telescope (UH88), the Astrophysical Research Consortium 3.5\u00a0m telescope (ARC), the 3.58\u00a0m Telescopio Nazionale Galileo (TNG), the Subaru 8.2\u00a0m telescope, and the Gemini North 8.1\u00a0m telescope, to confirm the lensing hypothesis of the four lensed quasar candidates. All the four candidates are doubly imaged lens candidates, and therefore their lensing hypothesis should be confirmed by both similar spectral energy distributions (SEDs) for the two stellar components and the existence of an extended object between the two components that act as a lens. We summarize the details of our follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations in Tables <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t2\">2</a> and\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t3\">3</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"aj494663t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table Multi-Object Spectrograph (GMOS) is installed on the Gemini telescope (North). The Device Optimized for the LOw RESolution (DOLORES) is installed on the TNG telescope.</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We clearly detect two stellar components in each original image of the follow-up imaging observations. Once we subtract two point spread functions (PSFs) using GALFIT (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r38\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r38\">2002</a>), we detect a significant residual, indicating an additional component in between the two PSFs, for all four systems. We then model the system with two PSFs plus an extended component represented by a S\u00e9rsic profile. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f2\">2</a>, an extended component is clearly visible after subtracting the two PSFs. The S\u00e9rsic parameters of the best-fitting model are summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t4\">4</a>. We also summarize the astrometric and photometric results for each system in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t5\">5</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Follow-up <em>I</em>-band images of the four lens systems. colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\"><em>z</em> = 20.73 \u00b1 0.51</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\"><em>K</em>' = 17.03 \u00b1 0.04</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small>\n<strong>Notes.</strong> Magnitudes are in the Vega system, except for <em>i</em>- and <em>z</em>-band which are in AB system. The <em>K</em>' band photometric zero point for SDSS J1515+1511 is less robust, as it is based on a single star in the field of view (non-photometric conditions), with catalog uncertainty 0.11\u00a0mag.</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t5_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t5_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>Results of the spectroscopic follow-up observations are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f3\">3</a>. For each candidate, we aligned the slit direction such that we can observe the two stellar components simultaneously. The good seeing condition (FWHM <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />0) enabled us to extract the spectrum of each component easily using standard IRAF<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#aj494663fn2\">10</a></sup> tasks. The spectra indicate that the SEDs of the two stellar components are quite similar for all four systems. In particular, the two quasar components of the SDSS J1405+0959 system have very similar broad absorption, which is in strong support of strong lensing interpretation of this system. The fainter component of SDSS J1515+1511 shows a strong Mg\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> absorption at ~5900\u2009\u00c5, which corresponds to an absorber at <em>z</em> = 0.742, and is likely to be associated with the lensing galaxy (see below).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Spectra of two lensed quasar images. The data between 5100\u2009\u00c5 and 5200\u2009\u00c5 for SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1128+2402 are excluded due to a gap of the detector. The wavelengths of quasar emission lines are indicated by vertical dotted lines. See Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t3\">3</a> for details of our spectroscopic follow-up observations.(Supplemental data of this figure are available in the <a href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663f3.tar.gz\" id=\"aj494663f3.tar.gz\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f3.tar.gz\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3\" data-art-data-content-type=\"Supplemental data\" data-art-data-type=\"supple-data\">online</a> journal.)</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-aj494663f3\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/downloadFigure/figure/aj494663f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-aj494663f3\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/downloadHRFigure/figure/aj494663f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"aj494663s3-2\" name=\"aj494663s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Lens Redshifts</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>First we examine our follow-up spectra carefully to look for any spectral signature of lensing galaxies. We find that the spectrum of the fainter component of SDSS J0743+2457 contains a significant amount of galaxy flux. We extract the spectrum of the lensing galaxy G by subtracting the spectrum of image A, with an appropriate offset corresponding to the flux ratio, from that of image B. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f4\">4</a> clearly indicates that the lensing galaxy is an early-type galaxy at <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> = 0.381.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Spectrum of the lensing galaxy G of SDSS J0743+2457. The spectrum clearly indicates that the lensing galaxy is an early-type galaxy at <em>z</em> = 0.381.(Supplemental data of this figure are available in the <a href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663f4.tar.gz\" id=\"aj494663f4.tar.gz\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f4.tar.gz\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4\" data-art-data-content-type=\"Supplemental data\" data-art-data-type=\"supple-data\">online</a> journal.)</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-aj494663f4\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/downloadFigure/figure/aj494663f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-aj494663f4\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/downloadHRFigure/figure/aj494663f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>For the other lens systems, we estimate redshifts of the lensing galaxies based on their colors. For SDSS J1405+0959, the S\u00e9rsic concentration index suggests that the residual may be a late-type galaxy. In this case, the <em>V</em>\u2009\u2212\u2009<em>R</em> and <em>R</em>\u2009\u2212\u2009<em>I</em> colors imply that the redshift is <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> ~ 0.5 (e.g., Fukugita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r17\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r17\">1995</a>). This is broadly consistent with <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> ~ 0.66 derived in Jackson et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r24\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r24\">2012</a>) using the overall spectral shape of the lensing galaxy in their follow-up spectroscopic data. For SDSS J1515+1511, the morphology is more robust in the <em>i</em>-band, where it is consistent with a late-type galaxy. Its color <em>i</em> \u2212 <em>K</em>' ~ 4.4 implies the redshift of <em>z</em> ~ 0.8\u20131.1, which is close to the redshift <em>z</em> = 0.742 of the strong absorber seen in the spectrum of the fainter quasar image. Thus we tentatively assign its lens redshift to be <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> = 0.742. It is difficult to estimate the photometric lens redshift of SDSS J1128+2402 from the current data.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s4\" name=\"aj494663s4\">4.\u00a0MASS MODELING</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We model the lens systems adopting a singular isothermal ellipsoid mass model using <em>glafic</em> (Oguri <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r33\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r33\">2010</a>). The number of parameters is eight (the position and flux of the source quasar, the position of the lensing galaxy, the Einstein radius, the ellipticity, and the position angle), while the number of constraints from the imaging observations is also eight (the positions and fluxes of the two quasar components, and the position of the lensing galaxy). Thus the model has zero degrees of freedom. We adopt the <em>I</em>-band imaging result as constraints for SDSS J0743+2457, SDSS J1128+2402, and SDSS J1405+0959. For SDSS J1515+1511, we use the <em>i</em>-band imaging result in spite of the lens being comparatively fainter, because the seeing was smaller, there were more stars available to build a PSF, and both astrometry and morphology are more robust. We summarize the parameters of the best-fitting (\u03c7<sup>2</sup> ~ 0) models in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t6\">6</a>. As is common (e.g., Keeton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r25\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r25\">1998</a>), there are large differences in the lensing galaxy shapes between the observations (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t4\">4</a>) and the best-fitting mass model parameters (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t6\">6</a>). This may partly be explained by nearby perturbers which affect the lens potentials.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"aj494663t6\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 6.</b>\u00a0Results of Mass Modeling</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663t6\" data-toolbar-img=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t6_lr.gif\" id=\"aj494663t6fn3\"></a><sup> c</sup> Total magnification factor predicted by the best fitting model.</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t6_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t6_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s5\" name=\"aj494663s5\">5.\u00a0SUMMARY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We have confirmed the lensing hypothesis for four lens candidates selected by the SQLS, based on the similar SEDs of the stellar components together with the existence of extended objects in between the stellar components, and the successful mass modeling of the observed configurations. All four are doubly imaged quasar lens systems: SDSS J0743+2457 (<em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.165, <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> = 0.381, \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />034), SDSS J1128+2402 (<em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 1.608, \u03b8 = 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />844), SDSS J1405+0959 (<em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 1.810, <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> ~ 0.66, \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />978), and SDSS J1515+1511 (<em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.054, <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> = 0.742, \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />989). Two of them (SDSS J1405+0959 and SDSS\u00a0J1515+1511) are included in the SQLS statistical sample (Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r22\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r22\">2012</a>) and are used for cosmological constraints (Oguri et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r35\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r35\">2012</a>).</p><p>These lens systems represent likely the last quasar lenses to emerge from the SQLS project. The applications of the SQLS lenses have been limited by the lack of high-resolution images for many of the SQLS lenses. We are therefore currently conducting a program to observe the SQLS lenses with Subaru telescope laser guide start adaptive optics system to accurately measure the quasar image positions and light profile of the lensing galaxy (Rusu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r42\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r42\">2011</a>; C. E. Rusu et al., in preparation). We are also carrying out a lensed quasar survey using the SDSS-III data (Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r14\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r14\">2011</a>) from which we will be able to discover more quasar lenses.</p></div><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>This work was supported in part by the FIRST program \"Subaru Measurements of Images and Redshifts (SuMIRe),\" World Premier International Research Center Initiative (WPI Initiative), MEXT, Japan, and Grant-in-Aid for Scientific Research from the JSPS (23740161). I.K. acknowledges support from MEXT KAKENHI 24740171. Use of the UH 2.2\u00a0m telescope for the observations is supported by NAOJ. Based in part on observations obtained with the Apache Point Observatory 3.5\u00a0m telescope, which is owned and operated by the Astrophysical Research Consortium, and on observations made with the Italian Telescopio Nazionale Galileo (TNG) operated on the island of La Palma by the Fundacion Galileo Galilei of the INAF (Istituto Nazionale di Astrofisica) at the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrofisica de Canarias. Based in part on observations obtained at the Gemini Observatory, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under a cooperative agreement with the NSF on behalf of the Gemini partnership: the National Science Foundation (United States), the National Research Council (Canada), CONICYT (Chile), the Australian Research Council (Australia), Minist\u00e9rio da Ci\u00eancia, Tecnologia e Inova\u00e7\u00e3o (Brazil) and Ministerio de Ciencia, Tecnolog\u00eda e Innovaci\u00f3n Productiva (Argentina).</p><p>Funding for the SDSS and SDSS-II has been provided by the Alfred P. Sloan Foundation, the Participating Institutions, the National Science Foundation, the U.S. Department of Energy, the National Aeronautics and Space Administration, the Japanese Monbukagakusho, the Max Planck Society, and the Higher Education Funding Council for England. The SDSS Web site is <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"url_link\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.sdss.org/\">http://www.sdss.org/</a>.</p><p>The SDSS is managed by the Astrophysical Research Consortium for the Participating Institutions. The Participating Institutions are the American Museum of Natural History, Astrophysical Institute Potsdam, University of Basel, Cambridge University, Case Western Reserve University, University of Chicago, Drexel University, Fermilab, the Institute for Advanced Study, the Japan Participation Group, Johns Hopkins University, the Joint Institute for Nuclear Astrophysics, the Kavli Institute for Particle Astrophysics and Cosmology, the Korean Scientist Group, the Chinese Academy of Sciences (LAMOST), Los Alamos National Laboratory, the Max-Planck-Institute for Astronomy (MPIA), the Max-Planck-Institute for Astrophysics (MPA), New Mexico State University, Ohio State University, University of Pittsburgh, University of Portsmouth, Princeton University, the United States Naval Observatory, and the University of Washington.</p></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/5759f22a-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/5759f22a-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">DISCOVERY OF FOUR DOUBLY IMAGED QUASAR LENSES FROM THE SLOAN DIGITAL SKY SURVEY</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Naohisa Inada</span><sup>1</sup></span>, <span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Masamune Oguri</span><sup>2,3</sup></span>, <span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Cristian E. class=\"da1 ta1\">\n                <!-- Start Linked Articles note -->\n\t<!-- End Linked Articles note -->\n<!-- Article information starts. This includes author emails, affiliations, article published date, doi etc. -->\n\t<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 wd-jnl-art-article-info-wrapper\">\n      \t<div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n        \t<a id=\"wd-article-info-accordion\" href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide article information\">Article information</a>\n      \t</div>\n      \t<div class=\"reveal-content\">\n        \t<div class=\"article-meta\">\n          \t\t<!-- Start Affiliations --><div class=\"wd-jnl-art-author-affiliations\"><div <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D1538-3881%2F147%2F6%2F153\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">1538-3881/147/6/153</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n                      <P>We report the discovery of four doubly imaged quasar lenses. All the four systems are selected as lensed quasar candidates from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey data. We confirm their lensing hypothesis with additional imaging and spectroscopic follow-up observations. The discovered lenses are SDSS J0743+2457 with the source redshift <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 2.165, the lens redshift <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> = 0.381, and the image separation \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />034, SDSS J1128+2402 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 1.608 and \u03b8 = 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />844, SDSS J1405+0959 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 1.810, <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> \u2248 0.66, and \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />978, and SDSS J1515+1511 with <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> = 2.054, <I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> = 0.742, and \u03b8 = 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />989. It is difficult to estimate the lens redshift of SDSS J1128+2402 from the current data. Two of the four systems (SDSS J1405+0959 and SDSS J1515+1511) are included in our final statistical lens sample to derive constraints on dark energy and the evolution of massive galaxies.</P>       </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=1538-3881/147/6/153&doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014AJ....147..153I\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2014AJ....147..153I&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2014AJ....147..153I\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/1538-3881/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s1\" name=\"aj494663s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Gravitationally lensed quasars have proven to be a useful tool for a variety of astrophysical and cosmological studies, as described e.g., in Kochanek (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r28\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r28\">2006</a>). Applications of quasar lenses include constraints on cosmological parameters and measurements of mass distributions for galaxy- and cluster-scale halos, interstellar medium associated with lensing or intervening galaxies, and the structure of quasar accretion disk and outflow (e.g., Fukugita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r15\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r15\">1990</a>; Kochanek <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r27\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r27\">1991</a>; Oguri et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r36\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r36\">2013</a>; Curran et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r11\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r11\">2007</a>; Poindexter et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r40\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r40\">2008</a>; Misawa et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r30\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r30\">2013</a>). The use of these quasar lenses can be enhanced by constructing a homogeneous lens sample with a well-characterized selection function. For instance, the Cosmic Lens All Sky Survey (Myers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r32\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r32\">2003</a>; Browne et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r9\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r9\">2003</a>) has provided a complete sample of 22 strong lenses selected among ~16,000 radio sources, which has been used for a number of cosmological and astrophysical studies (e.g., Chae et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r10\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r10\">2006</a>). Currently, we have completed the SDSS Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; Oguri et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r34\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r34\">2006</a>), which is the current largest lensed quasar survey using optical data of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS; York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r49\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r49\">2000</a>). The total number of lensed quasars identified in the SDSS data is 62<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#aj494663fn1\">9</a></sup> (Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r22\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r22\">2012</a>). The statistical analysis for SQLS lenses to constrain both cosmological parameters and the evolution of massive galaxies has been reported in Oguri et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r35\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r35\">2012</a>).</p><p>In this paper, we report the discovery of four lensed quasars from the SQLS. Since the description of the four lensed quasars in Inada et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r22\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r22\">2012</a>) is so brief, we show the detailed properties of the four systems here. We briefly describe the SDSS data and our algorithm to locate lensed quasar candidates in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s2\">2</a>. We then present follow-up observations to confirm their lensing hypotheses in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s3\">3</a>. We carry out mass modeling in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s4\">4</a>. Our result is summarized in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#aj494663s5\">5</a>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s2\" name=\"aj494663s2\">2.\u00a0CANDIDATE SELECTION FROM THE SLOAN DIGITAL SKY SURVEY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The SQLS identifies lensed quasars among ~100, 000 quasars (Schneider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r44\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r44\">2010</a>) from the SDSS Data Release 7 (DR7). The SDSS is a survey using a dedicated wide-field 2.5\u00a0m telescope (Gunn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r19\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r19\">2006</a>) at the Apache Point Observatory (New Mexico, USA) to conduct imaging and spectroscopic surveys for a quarter of the sky. The imaging data were obtained through five broad-band filters (<em>ugriz</em>; Fukugita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r16\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r16\">1996</a>; Gunn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r18\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r18\">1998</a>; Doi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r12\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r12\">2010</a>) with astrometric accuracy better than ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 (Pier et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r39\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r39\">2003</a>) and with photometric zeropoint accuracy better than ~0.01\u00a0mag (Hogg et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r20\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r20\">2001</a>; Smith et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r45\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r45\">2002</a>; Ivezi\u0107 et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r23\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r23\">2004</a>; Tucker et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r48\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r48\">2006</a>; Padmanabhan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r37\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r37\">2008</a>). Quasar and galaxy candidates were selected by the SDSS spectroscopic pipeline based on the imaging data (Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r13\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r13\">2001</a>; Richards et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r41\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r41\">2002</a>; Strauss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r47\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r47\">2002</a>). The candidates were tiled in each plate according to the algorithm of Blanton et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r8\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r8\">2003</a>), and were observed with multi-object fiber spectrographs (<em>R</em> ~ 1800) covering 3800\u20139200\u00a0\u00c5 (Blanton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r8\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r8\">2003</a>). The SDSS DR7 data have already been made public (Stoughton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r46\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r46\">2002</a>; Abazajian et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r1\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r1\">2003</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r2\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r2\">2004</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r3\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r3\">2005</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r4\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r4\">2009</a>; Adelman-McCarthy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r5\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r5\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r6\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r6\">2007</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r7\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r7\">2008</a>).</p><p>The procedure to identify lensed quasar candidates from the spectroscopic SDSS quasars has been described in the series of SQLS papers (e.g., Inada et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r21\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r21\">2008</a>), which we outline here. We use two selection methods. One is to find quasars with nearby objects whose colors are similar to the quasars. This method is tagged as the \"color selection.\" The color selection does not always work well for the SDSS data because of the relatively poor spatial resolution of SDSS imaging data, whose seeing sizes are comparable to typical image separations of quasar lenses. Therefore, in order to find lenses which are not deblended into multiple components in the SDSS data, we also exploit the so-called morphological selection, in which we select spectroscopic quasars with extended morphologies as lensed quasar candidates. SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1128+2402 are selected by the morphological selection, whereas SDSS J1405+0959 and SDSS J1515+1511 are selected by both the color selection and the morphological selection. The SDSS properties of these four candidates are summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t1\">1</a>. We also show the SDSS <em>i</em>-band images of the four objects in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f1\">1</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Finding charts (SDSS <em>i</em>-band images) of the four lens systems. wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We note that SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1405+0959 have been reported as quasar lenses ULAS 074352.6+245743 and ULAS 140515.4+095931, respectively, by the Major UKIDSS-SDSS Cosmic Lens Survey (MUSCLES) survey (Jackson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r24\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r24\">2012</a>). In the MUSCLES survey lens candidates are selected by cross-matching SDSS quasars with UKIDSS near-infrared images which typically have much better spatial resolution. Our identification of SDSS J0743+2457 and SDSS J1405+0959 as lens candidates is independent of the MUSCLES survey result.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"aj494663s3\" name=\"aj494663s3\">3.\u00a0FOLLOW-UP IMAGING AND SPECTROSCOPY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"aj494663s3-1\" name=\"aj494663s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Follow-up Data</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We carried out follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations using the University of Hawaii 2.2\u00a0m telescope (UH88), the Astrophysical Research Consortium 3.5\u00a0m telescope (ARC), the 3.58\u00a0m Telescopio Nazionale Galileo (TNG), the Subaru 8.2\u00a0m telescope, and the Gemini North 8.1\u00a0m telescope, to confirm the lensing hypothesis of the four lensed quasar candidates. All the four candidates are doubly imaged lens candidates, and therefore their lensing hypothesis should be confirmed by both similar spectral energy distributions (SEDs) for the two stellar components and the existence of an extended object between the two components that act as a lens. We summarize the details of our follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations in Tables <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t2\">2</a> and\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t3\">3</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"aj494663t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table The Device Optimized for the LOw RESolution (DOLORES) is installed on the TNG telescope.</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-6256/147/6/153\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/147/6/153/suppdata/aj494663t3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We clearly detect two stellar components in each original image of the follow-up imaging observations. Once we subtract two point spread functions (PSFs) using GALFIT (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#aj494663r38\" id=\"fnref-aj494663r38\">2002</a>), we detect a significant residual, indicating an additional component in between the two PSFs, for all four systems. We then model the system with two PSFs plus an extended component represented by a S\u00e9rsic profile. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#aj494663f2\">2</a>, an extended component is clearly visible after subtracting the two PSFs. The S\u00e9rsic parameters of the best-fitting model are summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t4\">4</a>. We also summarize the astrometric and photometric results for each system in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t5\">5</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"aj494663f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"aj494663f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/147/6/153/Full/aj494663f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Follow-up <em>I</em>-band images of the four lens systems. The images of SDSS J0743+2457, SDSS J1128+2402, and SDSS J1515+1511 were taken with UH88/Tek2k (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />22\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>), and the image of SDSS J1405+0959 were taken with UH88/8k (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />235\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>). North is up and east is left. For each system, the left panel shows the original image and the right panel shows the image after subtracting two PSF components. The residuals in the right panels are all fitted well by the S\u00e9rsic profile. See Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#aj494663t4\">4</a> for the fitting results.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn
